//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Fakaofo_Satellite_NASA.jpg/440px-Fakaofo_Satellite_NASA.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3032" data-file-height="2004" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Fakaofo_Satellite_NASA.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Fakaofo atoll</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bowditch_Tokelau.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Bowditch_Tokelau.png/220px-Bowditch_Tokelau.png" width="220" height="161" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Bowditch_Tokelau.png/330px-Bowditch_Tokelau.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Bowditch_Tokelau.png/440px-Bowditch_Tokelau.png 2x" data-file-width="462" data-file-height="339" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bowditch_Tokelau.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Fakaofo islanders, drawn in 1841 by the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Exploring_Expedition" title="United States Exploring Expedition">United States Exploring Expedition</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p><b>Tokelau</b> (previously known as the <b>Union Islands</b>, and officially as <b>Tokelau Islands</b> until 1976;<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> <span class="nowrap"><small>English:  </small><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/\xcb\x88/: primary stress follows">\xcb\x88</span><span title="&#39;t&#39; in &#39;tie&#39;">t</span><span title="/o\xca\x8a/: &#39;o&#39; in &#39;code&#39;">o\xca\x8a</span><span title="&#39;k&#39; in &#39;kind&#39;">k</span><span title="/\xc9\x99/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">\xc9\x99</span><span title="&#39;l&#39; in &#39;lie&#39;">l</span><span title="/a\xca\x8a/: &#39;ou&#39; in &#39;mouth&#39;">a\xca\x8a</span></span>/</a></span></span>; lit. "<a href="/wiki/North-northeast" class="mw-redirect" title="North-northeast">north-northeast</a>"<sup id="cite_ref-:3_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>) is a <a href="/wiki/Dependent_territory" title="Dependent territory">dependent territory</a> of <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a> in the southern Pacific Ocean. It consists of three tropical coral <a href="/wiki/Atoll" title="Atoll">atolls</a> (<a href="/wiki/Atafu" title="Atafu">Atafu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nukunonu" title="Nukunonu">Nukunonu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fakaofo" title="Fakaofo">Fakaofo</a>), with a combined land area of 10&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (4&#160;sq&#160;mi). The capital rotates yearly between the three atolls.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> Tokelau lies north of the <a href="/wiki/Samoan_Islands" title="Samoan Islands">Samoan Islands</a>, east of <a href="/wiki/Tuvalu" title="Tuvalu">Tuvalu</a>, south of the <a href="/wiki/Phoenix_Islands" title="Phoenix Islands">Phoenix Islands</a>, southwest of the more distant <a href="/wiki/Line_Islands" title="Line Islands">Line Islands</a>, and northwest of the <a href="/wiki/Cook_Islands" title="Cook Islands">Cook Islands</a>. <a href="/wiki/Swains_Island" title="Swains Island">Swains Island</a> is geographically part of Tokelau, but is subject to an ongoing territorial dispute and is currently administered by the United States as part of <a href="/wiki/American_Samoa" title="American Samoa">American Samoa</a>.\n</p><p>Tokelau has a population of approximately 1,500 people, the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_and_dependencies_by_population#Sovereign_states_and_dependencies_by_population" title="List of countries and dependencies by population">fourth-smallest population</a> of any sovereign state or dependency. As of the 2016 census, around 45% of residents <a href="/wiki/List_of_sovereign_states_and_dependent_territories_by_immigrant_population" title="List of sovereign states and dependent territories by immigrant population">were born overseas</a>, mostly in Samoa and New Zealand.<sup id="cite_ref-tokelau.org.nz_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tokelau.org.nz-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> The country has a <a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy" title="Life expectancy">life expectancy</a> of 69, comparable with other <a href="/wiki/Oceania" title="Oceania">Oceanian</a> island nations. Approximately 94% of the population speak <a href="/wiki/Tokelauan" class="mw-redirect" title="Tokelauan">Tokelauan</a> as a first language. The country has the smallest economy in the world, although it is a leader in <a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy" title="Renewable energy">renewable energy</a>, being the first 100% <a href="/wiki/Solar_power" title="Solar power">solar powered</a> nation in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Tokelau is officially referred to as a nation by both the New Zealand government and the Tokelauan government.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> It is a free and <a href="/wiki/Democracy" title="Democracy">democratic nation</a> with <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Tokelau" title="Politics of Tokelau">elections every three years</a>. However, in 2007 the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly" title="United Nations General Assembly">United Nations General Assembly</a> included Tokelau on its <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_list_of_Non-Self-Governing_Territories" title="United Nations list of Non-Self-Governing Territories">list of non-self-governing territories</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> Its inclusion on the list is controversial, as Tokelauans have twice voted against further self-determination and the islands\' small population reduces the viability of self-government. The basis of Tokelau\'s legislative, administrative and judicial systems is the Tokelau Islands Act 1948, which has been amended on a number of occasions. Since 1993, the territory has annually elected its own head of government, the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_Government_of_Tokelau" title="Head of Government of Tokelau"><i>Ulu-o-Tokelau</i></a>. Previously the <a href="/wiki/Administrator_of_Tokelau" title="Administrator of Tokelau">Administrator of Tokelau</a> was the highest official in the government and the territory was administered directly by a New Zealand government department.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-1 zone</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-4"><a href="#Government"><span class="tocnumber">3</span> <span class="toctext">Government</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 class="toclevel-2 tocsection-9"><a href="#Internet_domain_names"><span class="tocnumber">7.1</span> <span class="toctext">Internet domain names</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-10"><a href="#Solar_power"><span class="tocnumber">7.2</span> <span class="toctext">Solar power</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-11"><a href="#Demography"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">Demography</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-12"><a href="#Statistics"><span class="tocnumber">8.1</span> <span class="toctext">Statistics</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-13"><a href="#Culture"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">Culture</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-14"><a href="#Healthcare_and_education"><span class="tocnumber">9.1</span> <span class="toctext">Healthcare and education</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-15"><a href="#Sport"><span class="tocnumber">9.2</span> <span class="toctext">Sport</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-16"><a class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-19"><a href="#Further_reading"><span class="tocnumber">13</span> <span class="toctext">Further reading</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-20"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">14</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-21"><a href="#Governance"><span class="tocnumber">14.1</span> <span class="toctext">Governance</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-22"><a href="#Atolls"><span class="tocnumber">14.2</span> <span class="toctext">Atolls</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tokelau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The name <i>Tokelau</i> is a <a href="/wiki/Polynesian_languages" title="Polynesian languages">Polynesian</a> word meaning "north wind". The islands were named the <i>Union Islands</i> and <i>Union Group</i> by European explorers at an unknown time.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> <i>Tokelau Islands</i> was adopted as the name in 1946, and was contracted to <i>Tokelau</i> on 9 December 1976.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tokelau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Archaeological evidence indicates that the atolls of Tokelau \xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/Atafu" title="Atafu">Atafu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nukunonu" title="Nukunonu">Nukunonu</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Fakaofo" title="Fakaofo">Fakaofo</a> \xe2\x80\x93 were settled about 1,000 years ago and may have been a "nexus" into Eastern Polynesia.<sup id="cite_ref-Research_Coomons_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Research_Coomons-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> Inhabitants followed <a href="/wiki/Polynesian_mythology" class="mw-redirect" title="Polynesian mythology">Polynesian mythology</a> with the local god <a href="/wiki/Tui_Tokelau" title="Tui Tokelau">Tui Tokelau</a>; and developed forms of music (see <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Tokelau" title="Music of Tokelau">Music of Tokelau</a>) and art. The three atolls functioned largely independently while maintaining social and linguistic cohesion. Tokelauan society was governed by chiefly <a href="/wiki/Clan" title="Clan">clans</a>, and there were occasional inter-atoll skirmishes and wars as well as inter-marriage. Fakaofo, the "chiefly island",<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> held some dominance over Atafu and Nukunonu after the dispersal of Atafu. Life on the atolls was subsistence-based, with reliance on fish and <a href="/wiki/Coconut" title="Coconut">coconut</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-mfat_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mfat-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Commodore <a href="/wiki/John_Byron" title="John Byron">John Byron</a> discovered Atafu on 24 June 1765 and named it "Duke of York\'s Island". Parties onshore reported that there were no signs of current or previous inhabitants.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-mac30_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mac30-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Edward_Edwards_(Royal_Navy_officer)" title="Edward Edwards (Royal Navy officer)">Captain Edward Edwards</a>, knowing of Byron\'s discovery, visited Atafu on 6 June 1791<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2007)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> in search of the <a href="/wiki/Mutiny_on_the_Bounty" title="Mutiny on the Bounty"><i>Bounty</i> mutineers</a>. There were no permanent inhabitants, but houses contained canoes and fishing gear, suggesting the island was used as a temporary residence by fishing parties.<sup id="cite_ref-mac30_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mac30-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> On 12 June 1791, Edwards sailed southward and discovered Nukunonu, naming it "Duke of Clarence\'s Island".<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> A landing party could not make contact with the people but saw "<i>morai</i>s", burying places, and canoes with "stages in their middle" sailing across the lagoons.<sup id="cite_ref-mac30_19-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mac30-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>\nOn 29 October 1825 <a href="/w/index.php?title=August_R._Strong&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="August R. Strong (page does not exist)">August R. Strong</a> of the <a href="/wiki/USS_Dolphin_(1821)" title="USS Dolphin (1821)">USS&#160;<i>Dolphin</i>&#160;(1821)</a> ship wrote of his crew\'s arrival at the atoll Nukunonu: </p><blockquote><p>Upon examination, we found they had removed all the women and children from the settlement, which was quite small, and put them in canoes lying off a rock in the lagoon. They would frequently come near the shore, but when we approached they would pull off with great noise and precipitation.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote>\n<p>On 14 February 1835 Captain Smith of the United States <a href="/wiki/Whaling" title="Whaling">whaler</a> <i>General Jackson</i> records discovering Fakaofo, calling it "D\'Wolf\'s Island".<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-booklet_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-booklet-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> On 25 January 1841, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Exploring_Expedition" title="United States Exploring Expedition">United States Exploring Expedition</a> visited Atafu and discovered a small population living on the island. The residents appeared to be temporary, evidenced by the lack of a chief and the possession of double <a href="/wiki/Canoe" title="Canoe">canoes</a> (used for inter-island travel). They desired to barter, and possessed blue beads and a plane-iron, indicating previous interaction with foreigners.  The expedition reached Nukunonu on 28 January 1841 but did not record any information about inhabitants. On 29 January 1841, the expedition discovered Fakaofo and named it "Bowditch".<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> The islanders were found to be similar in appearance and nature to those in Atafu.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Missionaries preached <a href="/wiki/Christianity_in_Tokelau" class="mw-redirect" title="Christianity in Tokelau">Christianity in Tokelau</a> from 1845 to the 1860s. French <a href="/wiki/Catholic" class="mw-redirect" title="Catholic">Catholic</a> missionaries on <a href="/wiki/Wallis_Island" class="mw-redirect" title="Wallis Island">Wallis Island</a> (also known as \'Uvea) and missionaries of the <a href="/wiki/Protestant" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestant">Protestant</a> <a href="/wiki/London_Missionary_Society" title="London Missionary Society">London Missionary Society</a> in Samoa used native teachers to convert the Tokelauans. Atafu was converted to Protestantism by the London Missionary Society, Nukunonu was converted to Catholicism and Fakaofo was converted to both denominations.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Helped by <a href="/wiki/Swains_Island" title="Swains Island">Swains Island</a>-based Eli Jennings senior, <a href="/wiki/Peru" title="Peru">Peruvian</a> <a href="/wiki/Blackbirding" title="Blackbirding">"blackbird"</a>  <a href="/wiki/Slave_trader" class="mw-redirect" title="Slave trader">slave traders</a> arrived in 1863 and kidnapped nearly all (253) of the able-bodied men to work as labourers, depopulating the atolls.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> The Tokelauan men died of <a href="/wiki/Dysentery" title="Dysentery">dysentery</a> and <a href="/wiki/Smallpox" title="Smallpox">smallpox</a>, and very few returned. With this loss, the system of governance became based on the "Taupulega", or "Councils of Elders", where individual families on each atoll were represented.<sup id="cite_ref-mfat_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mfat-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-booklet_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-booklet-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> During this time, <a href="/wiki/Polynesia" title="Polynesia">Polynesian</a> immigrants and American, <a href="/wiki/Scottish_people" title="Scottish people">Scottish</a>, French, <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_people" title="Portuguese people">Portuguese</a> and German <a href="/wiki/Beachcombing#Historical_usage" title="Beachcombing">beachcombers</a> settled, marrying local women and repopulating the atolls.<sup id="cite_ref-booklet_23-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-booklet-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Between 1856 and 1979, the United States claimed that it held sovereignty over the island and the other Tokelauan atolls. In 1979, the U.S. conceded that Tokelau was under New Zealand sovereignty, and a <a href="/wiki/Maritime_boundary" title="Maritime boundary">maritime boundary</a> between Tokelau and <a href="/wiki/American_Samoa" title="American Samoa">American Samoa</a> was established by the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Tokehega" title="Treaty of Tokehega">Treaty of Tokehega</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Fakaofo_village_square_20070716.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Fakaofo village square 20070716.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Fakaofo_village_square_20070716.jpg/220px-Fakaofo_village_square_20070716.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Fakaofo_village_square_20070716.jpg/330px-Fakaofo_village_square_20070716.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Fakaofo_village_square_20070716.jpg/440px-Fakaofo_village_square_20070716.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2560" data-file-height="1920" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Fakaofo_village_square_20070716.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div></div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Cyclone_Percy" title="Cyclone Percy">Cyclone Percy</a> struck and severely damaged Tokelau in late February and early March 2005. Forecasters underestimated the cyclone\'s strength and the length of time it would be in vicinity to Tokelau. It coincided with a spring <a href="/wiki/Tide" title="Tide">tide</a> which put most of the area of the two villages on Fakaofo and Nukunonu under a metre of seawater. The cyclone also caused major <a href="/wiki/Erosion" title="Erosion">erosion</a> on several islets of all three atolls, damaging roads and bridges and disrupting electric power and telecommunications systems. The cyclone did significant and widespread damage to food crops including bananas, <a href="/wiki/Coconut" title="Coconut">coconuts</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pandanus" title="Pandanus">pandanus</a>. It did not seriously injure anyone but villagers lost significant amounts of property. The geographic future of Tokelau depends on the height of sea level.\n</p><p>No significant land is more than two metres (6.6 feet) above <a href="/wiki/High_water" class="mw-redirect" title="High water">high water</a> of ordinary tides. This means Tokelau is particularly vulnerable to any possible <a href="/wiki/Sea_level_rise" title="Sea level rise">sea level rises</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Time_zone">Time zone</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tokelau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Time zone">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Time_in_New_Zealand" title="Time in New Zealand">Time in New Zealand</a></div>\n<p>Until December 2011, Tokelau was 11&#160;hours behind <a href="/wiki/Coordinated_Universal_Time" title="Coordinated Universal Time">Coordinated Universal Time</a> (UTC).<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> At midnight 29 December 2011 Tokelau shifted to <a href="/wiki/UTC%2B13:00" title="UTC+13:00">UTC+13:00</a> in response to Samoa\'s decision to switch sides of the International Dateline.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> This brought Tokelau closer to <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a> time (and in the process omitted 30 December).<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Many sources claim that Tokelau is 14&#160;hours ahead of UTC (UTC \xe2\x88\x9210 before the 2011 date switch), but the correct time zone offset is UTC+13:00.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government">Government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tokelau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_history_of_Tokelau" title="Constitutional history of Tokelau">Constitutional history of Tokelau</a></div>\n<p>In 1877, the islands were included under the protection of the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_Great_Britain_and_Ireland" title="United Kingdom of Great Britain and Ireland">United Kingdom</a> by an <a href="/wiki/Order_in_Council" title="Order in Council">Order in Council</a> that claimed jurisdiction over all unclaimed <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Islands" title="Pacific Islands">Pacific Islands</a>. Commander C. F. Oldham on <a href="/wiki/HMS_Egeria_(1873)" title="HMS Egeria (1873)">HMS <i>Egeria</i></a> landed at each of the three atolls in June 1889<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> and officially raised the <a href="/wiki/Union_Flag" class="mw-redirect" title="Union Flag">Union Flag</a>, declaring the group a British <a href="/wiki/Protectorate" title="Protectorate">protectorate</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Colonial_Law&#39;_1966._P._894_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Colonial_Law&#39;_1966._P._894-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> In conformity with desire expressed by "the Native government" they were annexed by the United Kingdom and included in the <a href="/wiki/Gilbert_Islands" title="Gilbert Islands">Gilbert Islands</a> by the Tokelau Islands (Union Islands) Order in Council, 1916.<sup id="cite_ref-Colonial_Law&#39;_1966._P._894_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Colonial_Law&#39;_1966._P._894-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> The annexation took place on 29 February 1916.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> From the point in time that the islands were annexed, their people had the status of <a href="/wiki/British_subjects" class="mw-redirect" title="British subjects">British subjects</a>. Tokelau was removed from the <a href="/wiki/Gilbert_and_Ellice_Islands_Colony" class="mw-redirect" title="Gilbert and Ellice Islands Colony">Gilbert and Ellice Islands Colony</a> and placed under the jurisdiction of the <a href="/wiki/Governor-General_of_New_Zealand" title="Governor-General of New Zealand">Governor-General of New Zealand</a> in 1925, two Orders in Council being made for the purpose on the same day.<sup id="cite_ref-Colonial_Law&#39;_1966._P._894_33-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Colonial_Law&#39;_1966._P._894-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> This step meant that New Zealand took over administration of Tokelau from the British on 11 February 1926.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> At this point, Tokelau was still a territory under the sovereignty of the United Kingdom but administered by New Zealand.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Union Islands (Revocation) Order in Council, 1948<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> after reciting the agreement by the governments of the United Kingdom and New Zealand that the islands should become part of New Zealand, revoked the Union Islands (No. 2) Order in Council, 1925, with effect from a date fixed by the Governor-General of New Zealand after he was satisfied that the New Zealand Parliament had provided for the incorporation of the islands with New Zealand, as it did by the <i>Tokelau Islands Act 1948</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> Tokelau formally became part of New Zealand on 1 January 1949.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_37-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Dominion_of_New_Zealand" title="Dominion of New Zealand">Dominion of New Zealand</a>, of which Tokelau formerly was a part, has since been superseded by the <a href="/wiki/Realm_of_New_Zealand" title="Realm of New Zealand">Realm of New Zealand</a>, of which Tokelau remains a part. Defence is the responsibility of New Zealand. When the <i>British Nationality and New Zealand Citizenship Act 1948</i> came into effect on 1 January 1949, Tokelauans who were British subjects gained <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand_citizenship" class="mw-redirect" title="New Zealand citizenship">New Zealand citizenship</a>; a status they still hold.<sup id="cite_ref-Aliens_and_citizens_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Aliens_and_citizens-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Villages are entitled to enact their own laws regulating their daily lives and New Zealand law only applies where it has been extended by specific enactment. Serious crime is rare and there are no prisons, and offenders are publicly rebuked, fined or made to work.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tokelau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Tokelau" title="Politics of Tokelau">Politics of Tokelau</a></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a> is <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II_of_the_United_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="Elizabeth II of the United Kingdom">Elizabeth II</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_in_New_Zealand" class="mw-redirect" title="Monarchy in New Zealand">Queen in right of New Zealand</a>, who also reigns over the other <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_realm" title="Commonwealth realm">Commonwealth realms</a>. The Queen is represented in the territory by Administrator <a href="/wiki/Ross_Ardern" title="Ross Ardern">Ross Ardern</a>, the father of Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Jacinda_Ardern" title="Jacinda Ardern">Jacinda Ardern</a>. The current head of government is <a href="/wiki/Afega_Gaualofa" title="Afega Gaualofa">Afega Gaualofa</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Ulu_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ulu-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> who presides over the <a href="/wiki/Council_for_the_Ongoing_Government_of_Tokelau" title="Council for the Ongoing Government of Tokelau">Council for the Ongoing Government of Tokelau</a>, which functions as a cabinet. The Council consists of the <i>faipule</i> (leader) and <i>pulenuku</i> (village mayor) of each of the three atolls.<sup id="cite_ref-TokelauCouncilGovernance_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TokelauCouncilGovernance-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Administrator_of_Tokelau" title="Administrator of Tokelau">Administrator</a> is appointed by the <a href="/wiki/Minister_of_Foreign_Affairs_(New_Zealand)" title="Minister of Foreign Affairs (New Zealand)">Minister of Foreign Affairs and Trade</a> of New Zealand, and the office of <a href="/wiki/List_of_heads_of_government_of_Tokelau" class="mw-redirect" title="List of heads of government of Tokelau">Head of Government</a> rotates between the three <i>faipule</i> for a one-year term.<sup id="cite_ref-TokelauCouncilGovernance_42-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TokelauCouncilGovernance-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Tokelau Amendment Act of 1996 confers legislative power on the General Fono, a <a href="/wiki/Unicameralism" title="Unicameralism">unicameral</a> body. The number of seats each atoll receives in the Fono is determined by population \xe2\x80\x93 at present, Fakaofo and Atafu each have seven and Nukunonu has six.<sup id="cite_ref-TokelauCouncilGovernance_42-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TokelauCouncilGovernance-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> <i>Faipule</i> and <i>pulenuku</i> also sit in the Fono.<sup id="cite_ref-TokelauCouncilGovernance_42-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TokelauCouncilGovernance-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 11 November 2004, Tokelau and New Zealand took steps to formulate a treaty that would turn Tokelau from a non-self-governing territory to a self-governing state in <a href="/wiki/Associated_state" title="Associated state">free association</a> with New Zealand. Besides the treaty, a United Nations-sponsored <a href="/wiki/Tokelauan_self-determination_referendum,_2006" title="Tokelauan self-determination referendum, 2006">referendum on self-determination</a> took place, with the three islands voting on successive days starting 13 February 2006. (Tokelauans in <a href="/wiki/Apia,_Samoa" class="mw-redirect" title="Apia, Samoa">Apia, Samoa</a>, voted on 11 February.)<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> Out of 581 votes cast, 349 were for Free Association, being short of the two-thirds majority required for the measure to pass.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> The referendum was profiled (somewhat light-heartedly) in the 1 May 2006 issue of <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_Yorker" title="The New Yorker">The New Yorker</a></i> magazine.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> A repeat <a href="/wiki/Tokelauan_self-determination_referendum,_2007" title="Tokelauan self-determination referendum, 2007">referendum took place on 20\xe2\x80\x9324 October 2007</a>, again narrowly failing to approve self-government. This time the vote was short by just 16 votes or 3%.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In May 2008, the United Nations\' Secretary General <a href="/wiki/Ban_Ki-moon" title="Ban Ki-moon">Ban Ki-moon</a> urged colonial powers "to complete the decolonization process in every one of the remaining 16 <a href="/wiki/Non-Self-Governing_Territories" class="mw-redirect" title="Non-Self-Governing Territories">Non-Self-Governing Territories</a>", including Tokelau.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> This led <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_Zealand_Herald" title="The New Zealand Herald">The New Zealand Herald</a></i> to comment that the United Nations was "apparently frustrated by two failed attempts to get Tokelau to vote for independence".<sup id="cite_ref-NZ_Herald_10510595_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NZ_Herald_10510595-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> In April 2008, speaking as leader of the <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand_National_Party" title="New Zealand National Party">National Party</a>, future New Zealand Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/John_Key" title="John Key">John Key</a> stated that New Zealand had "imposed two referenda on the people of the Tokelau Islands", and questioned "the accepted wisdom that small states should undergo a de-colonisation process".<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tokelau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Tokelau includes three atolls in the South Pacific Ocean between longitudes <a href="/wiki/171st_meridian_west" title="171st meridian west">171\xc2\xb0</a> and <a href="/wiki/173rd_meridian_west" title="173rd meridian west">173\xc2\xb0&#160;W</a> and between latitudes <a href="/wiki/8th_parallel_south" title="8th parallel south">8\xc2\xb0</a> and <a href="/wiki/10th_parallel_south" title="10th parallel south">10\xc2\xb0&#160;S</a>, about midway between Hawaii and New Zealand. They lie about 500 kilometres (311 miles) north of <a href="/wiki/Samoa" title="Samoa">Samoa</a>. The atolls are <a href="/wiki/Atafu" title="Atafu">Atafu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nukunonu" title="Nukunonu">Nukunonu</a>, both in a group of islands once called the Duke of Clarence Group, and <a href="/wiki/Fakaofo" title="Fakaofo">Fakaofo</a>, once Bowditch Island. Their combined land area is 10.8&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (4.2&#160;sq&#160;mi). The atolls each have <a href="/wiki/List_of_islands_of_Tokelau" title="List of islands of Tokelau">a number of coral islands</a>, where <a href="/wiki/List_of_villages_in_Tokelau" title="List of villages in Tokelau">the villages</a> are situated. The highest point of Tokelau is just 5 metres (16 feet) <a href="/wiki/Above_sea_level" class="mw-redirect" title="Above sea level">above sea level</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> There are no ports or harbours for large vessels, however, all three atolls have a jetty to and from which supplies and passengers are shipped.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> Tokelau lies in the Pacific <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone" title="Tropical cyclone">tropical cyclone</a> belt. A fourth island that is culturally, historically, and geographically, but not politically, part of the Tokelau chain is <a href="/wiki/Swains_Island" title="Swains Island">Swains Island</a> (Olohega), under United States control since about 1900 and administered as part of <a href="/wiki/American_Samoa" title="American Samoa">American Samoa</a> since 1925.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Swains Island was claimed by the United States pursuant to the <a href="/wiki/Guano_Islands_Act" title="Guano Islands Act">Guano Islands Act</a>, as were the other three islands of Tokelau; these claims were ceded to Tokelau by treaty in 1979. In the draft constitution of Tokelau subject to the Tokelauan self-determination referendum in 2006, Olohega was also claimed as a part of Tokelau, though the claim was surrendered in the same 1979 treaty. This established a clearly defined boundary between American Samoa and Tokelau.\n</p><p>Tokelau\'s claim to Swains is generally comparable to the <a href="/wiki/Marshall_Islands" title="Marshall Islands">Marshall Islands</a>\' claim to US-administered <a href="/wiki/Wake_Island" title="Wake Island">Wake Island</a>, but the re-emergence of this somewhat dormant issue has been an unintended result of the United Nations\' recent efforts to promote decolonisation in Tokelau. Tokelauans have proved somewhat reluctant to push their national identity in the political realm: recent decolonisation moves have mainly been driven from outside for ideological reasons. But at the same time, Tokelauans are reluctant to disown their common cultural identity with Swains Islanders who speak their language.\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable" style="width:320px; text-align:center;">\n<caption><a href="/wiki/Geographic_location" class="mw-redirect" title="Geographic location">Geographic locations</a> of Tokelau\'s atolls\n</caption>\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Atoll\n</th>\n<th>Coordinates\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Atafu" title="Atafu">Atafu</a>\n</td>\n<td><span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=Tokelau&amp;params=8_33_6_S_172_30_3_W_region:TK_type:adm2nd&amp;title=Atafu"><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">8\xc2\xb033\xe2\x80\xb26\xe2\x80\xb3S</span> <span class="longitude">172\xc2\xb030\xe2\x80\xb23\xe2\x80\xb3W</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">&#xfeff; / <span class="geo">-9.16833; -171.80972</span></span><span style="display:none">&#xfeff; (<span class="fn org">Nukunonu</span>)</span></span></span></a></span>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Fakaofo" title="Fakaofo">Fakaofo</a>\n</td>\n<td><span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=Tokelau&amp;params=9_21_55_S_171_12_54_W_region:TK_type:adm2nd&amp;title=Fakaofo"><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">9\xc2\xb021\xe2\x80\xb255\xe2\x80\xb3S</span> <span class="longitude">171\xc2\xb012\xe2\x80\xb254\xe2\x80\xb3W</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">&#xfeff; / &#xfeff;</span><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="vcard"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">9.36528\xc2\xb0S 171.21500\xc2\xb0W</span><span style="display:none">&#xfeff; / <span class="geo">-9.36528; -171.21500</span></span><span style="display:none">&#xfeff; (<span class="fn org">Fakaofo</span>)</span></span></span></a></span>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Environment">Environment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tokelau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Environment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_birds_of_Tokelau" title="List of birds of Tokelau">List of birds of Tokelau</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_mammals_of_Tokelau" title="List of mammals of Tokelau">List of mammals of Tokelau</a></div>\n<p>Tokelau is located in the Western Polynesian tropical moist forests <a href="/wiki/List_of_terrestrial_ecoregions_(WWF)" title="List of terrestrial ecoregions (WWF)">ecoregion</a>. Most of the original vegetation has been replaced by <a href="/wiki/Coconut" title="Coconut">coconut</a> plantations some of which have been abandoned and became scrubby forests. The atolls of Tokelau provide habitat for 38 indigenous plant species, over 150 insect species and 10 land crab species. One of the greatest threats to biodiversity is posed by introduced mammalian predators such as the <a href="/wiki/Polynesian_Rat" class="mw-redirect" title="Polynesian Rat">Polynesian Rat</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2011 Tokelau declared its entire <a href="/wiki/Exclusive_economic_zone" title="Exclusive economic zone">exclusive economic zone</a> of 319,031&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (123,179&#160;sq&#160;mi) a <a href="/wiki/Shark_sanctuary" title="Shark sanctuary">shark sanctuary</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tokelau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Update" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><img alt="Ambox current red.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/42px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png" width="42" height="34" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/63px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/84px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="360" data-file-height="290" /></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section needs to be <b>updated</b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please update this article to reflect recent events or newly available information.</span>  <small><i>(June 2017)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Nukunonu_Lagoon20070716.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Nukunonu_Lagoon20070716.jpg/220px-Nukunonu_Lagoon20070716.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Nukunonu_Lagoon20070716.jpg/330px-Nukunonu_Lagoon20070716.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Nukunonu_Lagoon20070716.jpg/440px-Nukunonu_Lagoon20070716.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2560" data-file-height="1920" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Nukunonu_Lagoon20070716.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Nukunonu" title="Nukunonu">Nukunonu</a> Lagoon in Tokelau.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Atafu_street_dawn_20070715.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Atafu_street_dawn_20070715.jpg/220px-Atafu_street_dawn_20070715.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Atafu_street_dawn_20070715.jpg/330px-Atafu_street_dawn_20070715.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Atafu_street_dawn_20070715.jpg/440px-Atafu_street_dawn_20070715.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2560" data-file-height="1920" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Atafu_street_dawn_20070715.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Atafu street at dawn</div></div></div>\n<p>According to the US <a href="/wiki/Central_Intelligence_Agency" title="Central Intelligence Agency">Central Intelligence Agency</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(PPP)" title="List of countries by GDP (PPP)">list of countries by GDP (PPP)</a> Tokelau has the smallest economy of any country in the world. Tokelau has an annual <a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power" title="Purchasing power">purchasing power</a> of about <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">US$</a>1,000 (<a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">\xe2\x82\xac</a>674) per capita. The government is almost entirely dependent on <a href="/wiki/Subsidy" title="Subsidy">subsidies</a> from New Zealand. It has annual revenues of less than US$500,000 (\xe2\x82\xac336,995) against expenditures of some US$2.8 million (\xe2\x82\xac1.9 million). The deficit is made up by aid from New Zealand.\n</p><p>Tokelau annually exports around US$100,000 (\xe2\x82\xac67,000) of <a href="/wiki/Postage_stamp" title="Postage stamp">stamps</a>, <a href="/wiki/Copra" title="Copra">copra</a> and woven and carved handicrafts and imports over US$300,000 (\xe2\x82\xac202,000) of foodstuffs, building materials, and fuel to, and from, New Zealand. New Zealand also pays directly for the cost of medical and education services. Local industries include small-scale enterprises for <a href="/wiki/Copra" title="Copra">copra</a> production, wood work, plaited craft goods, stamps, coins, and fishing. Agriculture and livestock produces <a href="/wiki/Coconut" title="Coconut">coconuts</a>, copra, <a href="/wiki/Breadfruit" title="Breadfruit">breadfruit</a>, <a href="/wiki/Papaya" title="Papaya">papayas</a>, bananas, <a href="/wiki/Common_fig" title="Common fig">figs</a>, pigs, poultry and a few goats. Many Tokelauans live in New Zealand and support their families in Tokelau through <a href="/wiki/Remittance" title="Remittance">remittances</a>.\n</p><p>Tokelau is currently the world\'s only country to only use renewable sources of energy in the production and consumption of electricity.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> Tokelau\'s electricity is 93% generated by <a href="/wiki/Photovoltaic" class="mw-redirect" title="Photovoltaic">photovoltaics</a>, with the remainder generated from <a href="/wiki/Coconut_oil" title="Coconut oil">coconut oil</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> The goal of 100% renewable energy was met on 7 November 2012, according to the <a href="/wiki/Foreign_Affairs_Minister_of_New_Zealand" class="mw-redirect" title="Foreign Affairs Minister of New Zealand">Foreign Affairs Minister of New Zealand</a>, <a href="/wiki/Murray_McCully" title="Murray McCully">Murray McCully</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Internet_domain_names">Internet domain names</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tokelau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Internet domain names">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:TokelauInternetByAtoll2011.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/TokelauInternetByAtoll2011.png/220px-TokelauInternetByAtoll2011.png" width="220" height="136" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/TokelauInternetByAtoll2011.png/330px-TokelauInternetByAtoll2011.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/TokelauInternetByAtoll2011.png/440px-TokelauInternetByAtoll2011.png 2x" data-file-width="584" data-file-height="361" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:TokelauInternetByAtoll2011.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Access to internet in Tokelau, 2011</div></div></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/.tk" title=".tk">.tk</a></div>\n<p>Tokelau has increased its GDP by more than 10% through registrations of <a href="/wiki/Domain_name" title="Domain name">domain names</a> under its <a href="/wiki/Top-level_domain" title="Top-level domain">top-level domain</a>, <a href="/wiki/.tk" title=".tk">.tk</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> Registrations can be either free, in which case the user owns only usage rights and not the domain itself, or paid, which grants full rights. Free domains are pointed to Tokelau <a href="/wiki/Name_server" title="Name server">name servers</a>, which redirects the domain via <a href="/wiki/HTML" title="HTML">HTML</a> frames to a specified address or to a specified <a href="/wiki/A_record" class="mw-redirect" title="A record">A</a> or <a href="/wiki/NS_record" class="mw-redirect" title="NS record">NS record</a>, and the redirection of up to 250 email addresses to an external address (not at a .tk domain).\n</p><p>In September 2003 <a href="/wiki/Fakaofo" title="Fakaofo">Fakaofo</a> became the first part of Tokelau with a high-speed Internet connection. Foundation Tokelau financed the project. Tokelau gives most domain names under its authority away to anyone for free to gain publicity for the territory. This has allowed the nation to gain enhanced telecommunications technologies, such as more computers and Internet access for Tokelauan residents. By 2012, there were about 120 computers, mostly laptops, and 1/6th of the economy consists of income from .tk domain names.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>According to a 2016 analysis of domain name registration performed by the <a href="/wiki/.uk" title=".uk">.uk</a> registrar <a href="/wiki/Nominet" class="mw-redirect" title="Nominet">Nominet</a> using data from ZookNIC,.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> tk domains are the "world\'s largest country-code domain ... almost as large as second and third place holders China (<a href="/wiki/.cn" title=".cn">.cn</a>) and Germany (<a href="/wiki/.de" title=".de">.de</a>) combined".<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Solar_power">Solar power</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tokelau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Solar power">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Three <a href="/wiki/Solar_power" title="Solar power">solar power</a> stations provide 100% of current electrical demand from <a href="/wiki/Photovoltaics" title="Photovoltaics">photovoltaics</a>, with battery backup. The first power station was completed in August 2012. In total, 4,032 solar panels are used and 1,344 batteries weighing 250 kilograms (550&#160;lb)&#160;each, making Tokelau the first nation in the world to be 100% powered by solar power. The systems are designed to withstand winds of 230&#160;km/h (143&#160;mph). Previously electricity was generated using diesel generators, and was only available about 16&#160;hours/day.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demography">Demography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tokelau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Demography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:LanguagesSpokenTokelau2011.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/LanguagesSpokenTokelau2011.png/220px-LanguagesSpokenTokelau2011.png" width="220" height="149" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/LanguagesSpokenTokelau2011.png/330px-LanguagesSpokenTokelau2011.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/LanguagesSpokenTokelau2011.png/440px-LanguagesSpokenTokelau2011.png 2x" data-file-width="509" data-file-height="345" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:LanguagesSpokenTokelau2011.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Language statistics in Tokelau, 2006 and 2011</div></div></div>\n<p>According to the 2016 Tokelau Census, Tokelau has a <i><a href="/wiki/De_jure" title="De jure">de jure</a></i> usually resident population of 1,499 people. The census shows a 6.2% increase in the de jure usually resident population between 2011 and 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The nationals of Tokelau are called <a href="/w/index.php?title=Tokelauan_people&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Tokelauan people (page does not exist)">Tokelauans</a>, and the major ethnic group is <a href="/wiki/Polynesian_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Polynesian people">Polynesian</a>. The country has no minorities. The major religion is the <a href="/wiki/Congregational_Christian_Church" class="mw-redirect" title="Congregational Christian Church">Congregational Christian Church</a> and the main language is <a href="/wiki/Tokelauan_language" title="Tokelauan language">Tokelauan</a>, but English is also spoken.\n</p><p>Tokelau has fewer than 1,500 <a href="/wiki/Polynesia#Cultures_of_Polynesia" title="Polynesia">Polynesian</a> inhabitants in three villages. Their isolation and lack of resources greatly limits economic development and confines agriculture to the subsistence level. The very limited natural resources and overcrowding are contributing to emigration to <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a> and <a href="/wiki/Samoa" title="Samoa">Samoa</a>. Depletion of <a href="/wiki/Tuna" title="Tuna">tuna</a> has made fishing for food more difficult.\n</p><p>A significant proportion (44.9% in 2016) of the population <a href="/wiki/List_of_sovereign_states_and_dependent_territories_by_immigrant_population" title="List of sovereign states and dependent territories by immigrant population">were born overseas</a>, mostly in Samoa (15.3% of total population) and New Zealand (11.5%)<sup id="cite_ref-tokelau.org.nz_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tokelau.org.nz-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On the island of <a href="/wiki/Atafu" title="Atafu">Atafu</a> almost all inhabitants are members of the Congregational Christian Church of Samoa. On <a href="/wiki/Nukunonu" title="Nukunonu">Nukunonu</a> almost all are <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic">Roman Catholic</a>. On <a href="/wiki/Fakaofo" title="Fakaofo">Fakaofo</a> both denominations are present with the Congregational Christian Church predominant. The total proportions are: Congregational Christian Church 62%, Roman Catholic 34%, other 5%.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>While slightly more females than males live on Atafu and Fakaofo, males make up 57% of Nukunonu residents.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> Only 9% of Tokelauans aged 40 or more have never been married.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> One-quarter of the population were born overseas; almost all the rest live on the same atoll they were born on.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> Most households own five or more pigs.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Despite its low income, Tokelau has a life expectancy of 69 years, comparable with other Oceania islands.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Statistics">Statistics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tokelau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Statistics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The following demographic statistics are from the <i><a href="/wiki/CIA_World_Factbook" class="mw-redirect" title="CIA World Factbook">CIA World Factbook</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-CIAPAPUANEWGUINEA_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIAPAPUANEWGUINEA-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> [to be updated from 2016 Census report: Profile of Tokelau]<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><b>Population</b>\n</p>\n<ul><li>1,499</li></ul>\n<p><b>Nationality</b>\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tokelauan_people&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Tokelauan people (page does not exist)">Tokelauan</a> 65.3%</li>\n<li>part Tokelauan/Samoan 8.7%</li>\n<li>part Tokelauan/Tuvaluan 6.9%</li>\n<li>part Tokelauan/other Pacific islander 1.9%</li>\n<li>part Tokelauan/<a href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups_in_Europe" title="Ethnic groups in Europe">European</a> 1%</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Samoans" title="Samoans">Samoan</a> 6.7%</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Tuvalu" title="Demographics of Tuvalu">Tuvaluan</a> 2.8%</li>\n<li>Other <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Islander" title="Pacific Islander">Pacific islander</a> 1.1%</li>\n<li>Other 5.1%</li>\n<li>Unspecified 0.4% (2011 est.)</li></ul>\n<p><b>Religions</b>\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Congregational_Christian_Church" class="mw-redirect" title="Congregational Christian Church">Congregational Christian Church</a> 58.2%</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Roman Catholic</a> 36.6%</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Presbyterian" class="mw-redirect" title="Presbyterian">Presbyterian</a> 1.8%</li>\n<li>Other <a href="/wiki/Christian" title="Christian">Christian</a> 2.8%</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Spiritualism" title="Spiritualism">Spiritualism</a> and <a href="/wiki/New_Age" title="New Age">New Age</a> 0.1%</li>\n<li>Unspecified 0.5%</li></ul>\n<p><b>Languages</b>\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Tokelauan_language" title="Tokelauan language">Tokelauan</a> 93.5% (a <a href="/wiki/Polynesian_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Polynesian language">Polynesian language</a>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a> 58.9%</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Samoan_language" title="Samoan language">Samoan</a> 45.5%</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Tuvaluan_language" title="Tuvaluan language">Tuvaluan</a> 11.6%</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Gilbertese_language" title="Gilbertese language">Kiribati</a> 2.7%</li>\n<li>Other 2.5%</li>\n<li>None 4.1%</li>\n<li>Unspecified 0.6%</li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tokelau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Healthcare_and_education">Healthcare and education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tokelau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Healthcare and education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:TokelauLiteracyByAge2011.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/TokelauLiteracyByAge2011.png/220px-TokelauLiteracyByAge2011.png" width="220" height="139" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/TokelauLiteracyByAge2011.png/330px-TokelauLiteracyByAge2011.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/TokelauLiteracyByAge2011.png/440px-TokelauLiteracyByAge2011.png 2x" data-file-width="622" data-file-height="394" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:TokelauLiteracyByAge2011.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Literacy by age in Tokelau, 2011 census</div></div></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Healthcare_in_Tokelau" class="mw-redirect" title="Healthcare in Tokelau">Healthcare in Tokelau</a></div>\n<p>Each atoll has a school and hospital. The health services have a Director of Health in <a href="/wiki/Apia" title="Apia">Apia</a> and a Chief Clinical Advisor who moves from atoll to atoll as required to assist the doctors attached to each hospital. In 2007 there was not always a doctor on each island and <a href="/wiki/Locum" title="Locum">locums</a> were appointed to fill the gaps. Upcoming Tokelaun medical graduates should alleviate this shortage in the coming years.\n</p><p>Many Tokelauan youth travel to New Zealand to further their education and the country is closer to full around Christmas time with students returning home and then heading off for another year of study.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tokelau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cricket,_Tokelau_Islands,_1966_(17501454372)_(2).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Cricket%2C_Tokelau_Islands%2C_1966_%2817501454372%29_%282%29.jpg/220px-Cricket%2C_Tokelau_Islands%2C_1966_%2817501454372%29_%282%29.jpg" width="220" height="166" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Cricket%2C_Tokelau_Islands%2C_1966_%2817501454372%29_%282%29.jpg/330px-Cricket%2C_Tokelau_Islands%2C_1966_%2817501454372%29_%282%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Cricket%2C_Tokelau_Islands%2C_1966_%2817501454372%29_%282%29.jpg/440px-Cricket%2C_Tokelau_Islands%2C_1966_%2817501454372%29_%282%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="680" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cricket,_Tokelau_Islands,_1966_(17501454372)_(2).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Cricket" title="Cricket">Cricket</a> in Tokelau, 1966</div></div></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union_in_Tokelau" title="Rugby union in Tokelau">Rugby union in Tokelau</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rugby_league_in_Tokelau" title="Rugby league in Tokelau">Rugby league in Tokelau</a></div>\n<p>Due to its small size, Tokelau is unaffiliated to most international sports organisations, and rarely takes part in international events. The only significant international competition the country takes part in is the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Games" title="Pacific Games">Pacific Games</a>. Tokelau won its first ever gold medals at the <a href="/wiki/2007_Pacific_Games" title="2007 Pacific Games">2007 Pacific Games</a> in <a href="/wiki/Apia" title="Apia">Apia</a>, winning a total of five medals (three gold, a silver and a bronze), all in <a href="/wiki/Lawn_bowls" class="mw-redirect" title="Lawn bowls">lawn bowls</a>, and finishing twelfth (out of twenty-two) on the overall medal table. This included two gold medals for <a href="/wiki/Violina_Linda_Pedro" title="Violina Linda Pedro">Violina Linda Pedro</a> (in the women\'s pairs and the women\'s singles), making her Tokelau\'s most successful individual athlete to date.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In October 2010, <a href="/wiki/Table_tennis" title="Table tennis">table tennis</a> became "the first sport in Tokelau to be granted membership at a Continental or World level", when the <a href="/wiki/Tokelau_Table_Tennis_Association" title="Tokelau Table Tennis Association">Tokelau Table Tennis Association</a> was formally established and became the 23rd member of the <a href="/wiki/Oceania_Table_Tennis_Federation" title="Oceania Table Tennis Federation">Oceania Table Tennis Federation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ittf.com_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ittf.com-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Tokelau was due to take part, for the first time, in the <a href="/wiki/2010_Commonwealth_Games" title="2010 Commonwealth Games">2010 Commonwealth Games</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Delhi" title="Delhi">Delhi</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> but, for unknown reasons, ultimately did not do so.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Tokelau does have a National Sports Federation, and the most important sports event within the country is arguably the Tokelau Games which are held yearly. When they are held, "all of Tokelau virtually stands still", as "[i]n excess of 50% of the population take part and all work and school stops at the time". The 2010 Games included competitions in <a href="/wiki/Rugby_sevens" title="Rugby sevens">rugby sevens</a>, <a href="/wiki/Netball" title="Netball">netball</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kilikiti" title="Kilikiti">kilikiti</a>, alongside "a cultural evening [...] where each atoll showcases their traditional songs and dances".<sup id="cite_ref-ittf.com_76-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ittf.com-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Netball" title="Netball">Netball</a> is thought to have been introduced to Tokelau by the British, but became more popular when New Zealand\'s government took over the territory. The sport is often played during inter-island sport competitions, alongside other sports like <a href="/wiki/Rugby_league" title="Rugby league">rugby league</a> and <a href="/wiki/Volleyball" title="Volleyball">volleyball</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In Tokelau, there are two levels to the <a href="/wiki/Soccer" class="mw-redirect" title="Soccer">soccer</a> league. From <a href="/wiki/Fale,_Tokelau" title="Fale, Tokelau">Fale</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fakaofo" title="Fakaofo">Fakaofo</a>, two of the best clubs are <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hakava_Club&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Hakava Club (page does not exist)">Hakava Club</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Matalele_Club&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Matalele Club (page does not exist)">Matalele Club</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-rsssf_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rsssf-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Communication_and_transportation">Communication and transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tokelau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Communication and transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tokelau_barge.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Tokelau_barge.JPG/220px-Tokelau_barge.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Tokelau_barge.JPG/330px-Tokelau_barge.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Tokelau_barge.JPG/440px-Tokelau_barge.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2560" data-file-height="1920" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tokelau_barge.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A barge leaves the landing ramp in <a href="/wiki/Nukunono" class="mw-redirect" title="Nukunono">Nukunono</a> to collect cargo and passengers from the MV <i>Tokelau</i></div></div></div>\n<p>Tokelau has a radio telephone service between the islands and to <a href="/wiki/Samoa" title="Samoa">Samoa</a>. In 1997, a government-regulated telephone service (TeleTok) with three satellite earth stations was established. Each atoll has a radio-broadcast station that broadcasts shipping and weather reports and every household has a radio or access to one. News is disseminated through the government <a href="/wiki/Newsletter" title="Newsletter">newsletter</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Te_Vakai" title="Te Vakai">Te Vakai</a></i>.\n</p><p>Tokelau has the <a href="/wiki/International_calling_code" class="mw-redirect" title="International calling code">international calling code</a> of 690, and has had five-digit telephone numbers from November 2015 (the existing four-digit numbers were prefixed by the digit "2")<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Tokelau is served by the MV <i>Mataliki</i>, delivered new in 2016 as a replacement of the smaller <i>MV Tokelau</i> and jointly managed by the Tokelau Transport Department and the company Transport and Marine. The vessel, which has a capacity of 60 passengers on international cruises and 120 for transport between the atolls of Tokelau, operates fortnightly between Tokelau and <a href="/wiki/Apia" title="Apia">Apia</a>, with the trip taking a little over a day.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> A dedicated cargo vessel, the <i>MV Kalopaga</i>, will enter service in 2018 and replace chartered freight vessels.<sup id="cite_ref-Radio_NZ_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Radio_NZ-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Ships load and unload cargo by motoring up to the down-wind (<a href="/wiki/Leeward" class="mw-redirect" title="Leeward">leeward</a>) side of the islet where the people live and maintaining station, by intermittent use of engines, close to the reef edge so that a landing barge can be motored out to transfer cargo to or from the shore. On returning to shore, the barge negotiates a narrow channel through the reef to the beach. Usually this landing is subject to ocean swell and beaching requires considerable skill and, often, <a href="/wiki/Coral" title="Coral">coral</a> abrasions to bodies. When bad weather prevents the barge making the trip, the ship stands off to wait for suitable weather or goes off to one of the other atolls to attempt to load or unload its passengers or cargo, or both.\n</p><p>There is no airport in Tokelau, so boats are the main means of travel and transport. Some <a href="/wiki/Seaplanes" class="mw-redirect" title="Seaplanes">seaplanes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Amphibious_aircraft" title="Amphibious aircraft">amphibious aircraft</a> are able to land in the island\'s lagoons.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> An airstrip was considered by the New Zealand Government in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> In 2016, plans to link the atolls with Samoa by helicopter had to be abandoned because of high costs, leading in the following years to renewed calls to the New Zealand government for help with establishing air services.<sup id="cite_ref-Radio_NZ_83-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Radio_NZ-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tokelau&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="navigation" Ministry for Culture and Heritage<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">27 August</span> 2016</span>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.jtitle=Te+Ara+%E2%80%93+the+Encyclopedia+of+New+Zealand&amp;rft.atitle=Citizenship+%E2%80%93+Aliens+and+citizens&amp;rft.date=2012-07-13&amp;rft.aulast=Green&amp;rft.aufirst=David&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.teara.govt.nz%2Fen%2Fcitizenship%2F3&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ATokelau" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-41"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-41">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20140220023040/http://tokelau.org.nz/">"Official site for the Tokelau Council of Ongoing Government"</a>. Archived from <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.tokelau.org.nz/">the original</a> on 20 February 2014<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">4 November</span> 2007</span>. <q>The legislation and judicial systems are based on the Tokelau Act, 1948, and its amendments. A major law reform project is continuing; its purpose is to ensure that Tokelau has a coherent body of law which responds to current needs and gives due recognition to local custom. Unless it is expressly extended to Tokelau, New Zealand statute law does not apply to the territory. In practice, no New Zealand legislation is extended to Tokelau without Tokelauan consent. The villages have the statutory power to enact their own laws covering village affairs. International covenants on economic, social and cultural rights and civil and political rights, ratified by New Zealand in December 1978, apply in Tokelau. Civil and criminal jurisdiction is exercised by commissioners and the New Zealand high court.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=Official+site+for+the+Tokelau+Council+of+Ongoing+Government&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.tokelau.org.nz%2F&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ATokelau" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-TokelauCouncilGovernance-42"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-TokelauCouncilGovernance_42-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-TokelauCouncilGovernance_42-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-TokelauCouncilGovernance_42-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-TokelauCouncilGovernance_42-3"><sup><i><b>d</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20130507092318/http://www.tokelau.org.nz/Tokelau+Government/Government/HOW+TOKELAU+IS+GOVERNED.html">"How Tokelau is Governed"</a>.
